<p>"<b>Can't Stop the Feeling!</b>" is a song recorded by American singer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a> for <a href="/wiki/Trolls_(soundtrack)" title="Trolls (soundtrack)">the soundtrack</a> to the film <i><a href="/wiki/Trolls_(film)" title="Trolls (film)">Trolls</a></i>, for which he serves as the executive music producer. It was written and produced by Timberlake, <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shellback_(record_producer)" title="Shellback (record producer)">Shellback</a>. Musically, it is an uptempo <a href="/wiki/Post-disco" title="Post-disco">disco-pop</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul-pop" title="Soul-pop">soul-pop</a> number with <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funk</a> influences. The song was released as a single on May 6, 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> and serviced to <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_hit_radio" title="Contemporary hit radio">contemporary hit radio</a> on May 10, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chr_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-chr-2">[2]</a></sup> Timberlake gave his first televised performance of "Can't Stop the Feeling!" during the interval act of the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2016" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2016">Eurovision Song Contest 2016</a> grand final. Directed by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Romanek" title="Mark Romanek">Mark Romanek</a>, its music video was released on May 16, 2016, and follows Timberlake on a tour to everyday places as he dances through what a typical day might be—it was followed by a number of fan-made videos.</p>
<p>The single debuted atop the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, opening with 379,000 downloads in its first week, marking Timberlake's fifth No. 1 single in the country, and making it the 26th song on the Hot 100 history to start at the summit of the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hot100numberone_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-hot100numberone-3">[3]</a></sup> Additionally, it became the second song to spend its first 10 weeks atop the <a href="/wiki/Digital_Songs" title="Digital Songs">Digital Songs</a> chart, joining <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">The Black Eyed Peas</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Boom_Boom_Pow" title="Boom Boom Pow">Boom Boom Pow</a>" (2009). The single marked his fifth No. 1 single on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay_(Radio_Songs)" title="Hot 100 Airplay (Radio Songs)">Radio Songs</a> chart and eighth on the <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a>. Internationally, it topped the charts in Argentina, Brazil, Belgium, Canada, the Czech Republic, France, Germany, Israel, Mexico, Russia, Scotland, Slovakia, Slovenia, South Africa, Sweden and Switzerland, and the top-five in most of Europe.</p>
<p>"Can't Stop the Feeling!" was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles_in_the_United_States" title="List of best-selling singles in the United States">best-selling song</a> of 2016 in the US with 2.49 million copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nielsen_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-nielsen-4">[4]</a></sup> For <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music" title="Apple Music">Apple Music</a> it was the second most streamed and downloaded song of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Official_Charts_Company" title="Official Charts Company">Official Charts Company</a> from the UK named it Timberlake's biggest song in the country, for over 1 million units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukhit_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukhit-6">[6]</a></sup> The song has received several awards and nominations. It was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song">Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldenglobe_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-goldenglobe-7">[7]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Critics%27_Choice_Movie_Award_for_Best_Song" title="Critics' Choice Movie Award for Best Song">Critics' Choice Award for Best Song</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cr_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-cr-8">[8]</a></sup> and is currently nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Academy Award for Best Original Song</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oscar_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-oscar-9">[9]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Song_Written_for_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media">Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammy_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_composition">Background and composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background and composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>

<div class="haudio">

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">A sample of "Can't Stop the Feeling!", a disco-pop song with funk influences.</div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In the early stages of recording his fifth studio album,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Timberlake also served as the executive music producer for the soundtrack to the film <i><a href="/wiki/Trolls_(film)" title="Trolls (film)">Trolls</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The uptempo <a href="/wiki/Post-disco" title="Post-disco">disco-pop</a> track was written and produced by Timberlake, <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shellback_(record_producer)" title="Shellback (record producer)">Shellback</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-techtime_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-techtime-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fuse_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-fuse-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> described the song as a "funky mix of disco and pop."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> For <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i> it is a "a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul-pop" title="Soul-pop">soul-pop</a> sugar rush tweaked for maximum dance grooves."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-avclub-18">[18]</a></sup> "Can't Stop the Feeling!" is written in the key of <a href="/wiki/C_major" title="C major">C major</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a> of 113 beats per minute. The song follows a chord progression of C – Am<small>7</small> – F<small>maj9</small> – Am<small>7</small>, and Timberlake's vocals span two octaves, from E<sub>4</sub> to E<sub>6</sub>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>[Fatherhood] changes everything. I don't know that [the song] was directly inspired to be something that my son could listen to of mine — because there’s a lot of music he can’t listen to of mine, at least not yet.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Timberlake talking about what influenced him to make the song in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Today_(U.S._TV_program)" title="Today (U.S. TV program)">Today</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>"Can't Stop the Feeling!" appears in the denouement of the movie, conceived with the idea of covering the <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> genre inspired by the situation of the scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thewrap_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-thewrap-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>What’s different about this is that it’s not even like writing just a song for a movie, it’s writing a song for characters who are going to sing it in the movie.That’s the part that made it a task that none of us had ever done. This is a modern animated musical, and we wanted to push ourselves to do something that worked in that way. I’m glad we did it, but none of it came easily.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Timberlake's reply to a question on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Wrap" title="The Wrap">The Wrap</a></i>, which said: "Are there more constraints to writing a song for a film that you don’t get when you’re writing for yourself?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thewrap_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-thewrap-21">[21]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical">Critical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Critical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Critical reception to the song has been mostly positive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cr_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-cr-8">[8]</a></sup> Writers from <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-13">[13]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-rolling-22">[22]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuse_TV" title="Fuse TV">Fuse</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fuse_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-fuse-15">[15]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> highlighted its attractiveness for the <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">summer season</a>. Adelle Platon from <i>Billboard</i> called it "delightful" and a "feel-good jam".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-13">[13]</a></sup> Nate Chinen from <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> wrote "Timberlake is on firm footing here, gliding over a <a href="/wiki/Post-disco" title="Post-disco">disco-pop</a> beat and urging all comers to catch the spirit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Jon Niles from <i>Music Times</i> wrote: "The song gives off a feeling of pure joy that only a talent as great as Timberlake could bring to the table."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> For Lisa Respers France of <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> Entertainment, "If Friday had a sound, it would be Justin Timberlake's "Can't Stop the Feeling!"."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Ed Masley wrote in <a href="/wiki/The_Arizona_Republic" title="The Arizona Republic">AZCentral</a> "the lyrics sound like they were custom-made to be the soundtrack to your favorite summer memories."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> For <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i>, Annie Zaleski wrote "a perfect summer song is one I can blast while driving in the car with the windows down. The tune doesn’t have to be meaningful—in fact, the more lightweight, the better—and it should offer a few minutes of unadulterated escapism. This year, I can already tell that “Can’t Stop The Feeling!” is my hot-weather jam."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-avclub-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i> included it among the 40 best songs of 2016 (first half).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> ranked "Can't Stop the Feeling!" at number 33 on their on their "100 Best Pop Songs of 2016" list, adding "the rhythm is eventually gonna get you to dance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a> considered it the 19th best pop song of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Idolator_(website)" title="Idolator (website)">Idolator</a> named it the 20th best song of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Timberlake received the Hollywood Song Award for "Can't Stop the Feeling!" at the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Film_Awards" title="Hollywood Film Awards">Hollywood Film Awards</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and won the award for Song in Animated Film at the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Music_in_Media_Awards" title="Hollywood Music in Media Awards">Hollywood Music in Media Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> It was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song">Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldenglobe_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-goldenglobe-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Critics%27_Choice_Movie_Award_for_Best_Song" title="Critics' Choice Movie Award for Best Song">Critics' Choice Award for Best Song</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cr_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-cr-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Satellite Award for Best Original Song">Satellite Award for Best Original Song</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and by the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Film_Critics_Society" title="Denver Film Critics Society">Denver Film Critics Society</a> for Best Original Song<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> and the Guild of Music Supervisors Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> It is currently nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Academy Award for Best Original Song</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oscar_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-oscar-9">[9]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Song_Written_for_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media">Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammy_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2016_Teen_Choice_Awards" title="2016 Teen Choice Awards">2016 Teen Choice Awards</a>, "Can't Stop the Feeling!" received nominations for Choice Summer Song, Choice Party Song and Choice Song from a Movie or TV Show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> It received a nomination for Song of the Summer at the <a href="/wiki/2016_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2016 MTV Video Music Awards">2016 MTV Video Music Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and International Song of the Year at the 2016 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NRJ_Music_Awards" title="NRJ Music Awards">NRJ Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BBC_Music_Awards" title="BBC Music Awards">BBC Music Awards</a> shortlisted it for Song of the Year nominee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> It later won the award for Favorite Song at the <a href="/wiki/43rd_People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="43rd People's Choice Awards">43rd People's Choice Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2017_iHeartRadio_Music_Awards" title="2017 iHeartRadio Music Awards">2017 iHeartRadio Music Awards</a> the song is nominated for Song of the Year and Best Song from a Movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iheartaward_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-iheartaward-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2016, <i>Billboard</i> named it the wedding DJs' 4th most popular party song in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The release of the song was followed by numerous fan-made videos, which also includes The <a href="/wiki/Memphis_Grizzlies" title="Memphis Grizzlies">Memphis Grizzlies</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viral_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-viral-44">[44]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Olympic_Committee" title="United States Olympic Committee">United States Olympic Committee</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> citizens of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memphis" title="Memphis">Memphis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gilbert,_Arizona" title="Gilbert, Arizona">Gilbert</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> graduates of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Milwaukee" title="University of Wisconsin–Milwaukee">University of Wisconsin–Milwaukee</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viral_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-viral-44">[44]</a></sup> among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> On May 26, 2016, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret_Angels" title="Victoria's Secret Angels">Victoria's Secret Angels</a> released a video in which they lip-synced to "Can't Stop the Feeling!".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Choreographers Celia Rowlson-Hall and Crishon Landers with the help of film producer Mia Lidofsky created a <a href="/wiki/Flash_mob" title="Flash mob">flash mob</a> <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">dance video</a> on October 2, 2016 in support of the <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton_presidential_campaign,_2016" title="Hillary Clinton presidential campaign, 2016">Hillary Clinton presidential campaign, 2016</a> set to the music of "Can't Stop the Feeling!" — with all of the dancers wearing <a href="/wiki/Pantsuit" title="Pantsuit">pantsuits</a> in reference to Hillary Clinton's outfit of choice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pantsuitpower_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-pantsuitpower-50">[50]</a></sup> They called the event #Pantsuitpower Flashmob for Hillary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pantsuitpower_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-pantsuitpower-50">[50]</a></sup> The video was covered in news media including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(magazine)" title="Vogue (magazine)">Vogue</a></i>, — and garnered over 2 million views on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pantsuitpower_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-pantsuitpower-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> From New York City, the Pantsuit Power movement then spread to <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh, North Carolina</a> on October 23, 2016 with another flash mob.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first video released, titled "First Listen", features cast members from the <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">DreamWorks Animation</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Trolls_(film)" title="Trolls (film)">Trolls</a></i>, among them <a href="/wiki/Anna_Kendrick" title="Anna Kendrick">Anna Kendrick</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Corden" title="James Corden">James Corden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icona_Pop" title="Icona Pop">Icona Pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Funches" title="Ron Funches">Ron Funches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kunal_Nayyar" title="Kunal Nayyar">Kunal Nayyar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-rolling-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cant_Stop_the_Feeling_music_video.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="376" data-file-width="505" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d2/Cant_Stop_the_Feeling_music_video.png/220px-Cant_Stop_the_Feeling_music_video.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d2/Cant_Stop_the_Feeling_music_video.png/330px-Cant_Stop_the_Feeling_music_video.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d2/Cant_Stop_the_Feeling_music_video.png/440px-Cant_Stop_the_Feeling_music_video.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cant_Stop_the_Feeling_music_video.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A screenshot from the clip showing the scene inspired by <i><a href="/wiki/Anchors_Aweigh_(film)" title="Anchors Aweigh (film)">Anchors Aweigh</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The song's official music video was released on May 16, 2016. Helmed by director <a href="/wiki/Mark_Romanek" title="Mark Romanek">Mark Romanek</a>, the "Can't Stop the Feeling!" video follows Timberlake on a tour to everyday places like a laundromat, diner, barbershop and a donut shop, with an individual dancing along to the single at every stop. All the revelers eventually end up congregating with Timberlake below a highway underpass where they dance together to the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> As described by <i><a href="/wiki/Time" title="Time">Time</a></i> editor Cady Lang, Timberlake "dances through what a typical day might be: breakfast at the diner and grocery shopping."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Talking to <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, director Mark Romanek described the concept as "just the overall feeling of unironic and sincere <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">humanism</a>. It’s not trying to be cool or slick or ironic. It’s just fun. Most of the time, people are excellent. It’s just a big sugar cookie. It makes people smile for four minutes." He stated the brief dance-off between Timberlake and an <a href="/wiki/Airdancer" title="Airdancer">inflatable arm waving tube man</a> was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Gene_Kelly" title="Gene Kelly">Gene Kelly</a> dancing with <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Mouse" title="Jerry Mouse">Jerry the mouse</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Anchors_Aweigh_(film)" title="Anchors Aweigh (film)">Anchors Aweigh</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Bustle_(magazine)" title="Bustle (magazine)">Bustle</a></i> writer Amy Mackelden highlighted the scene as the best moment of the video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Esquire_(magazine)" title="Esquire (magazine)">Esquire</a></i> editor Jonathan Evans addressed Timberlake's <a href="/wiki/Monochromatic_color" title="Monochromatic color">monochromatic</a> outfit, writing "the singer nails it by playing with shades of the color [white], plus throwing some pattern and texture in the mix."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The video received a nomination for <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_Japan_for_Best_Male_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award Japan for Best Male Video">Best Male Video International</a> at the 2016 <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards_Japan" title="MTV Video Music Awards Japan">MTV Video Music Awards Japan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and is nominated for Best Music Video at the <a href="/wiki/2017_iHeartRadio_Music_Awards" title="2017 iHeartRadio Music Awards">2017 iHeartRadio Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iheartaward_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-iheartaward-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performance">Live performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Live performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On May 9, 2016, it was announced that Timberlake would be performing his song during the interval act of the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2016" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2016">Eurovision Song Contest 2016</a> finale, which took place in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> on May 14, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> This was the first time in the contest's history whereby a celebrated artist who had never participated in the contest performed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Timberlake opened the performance singing "<a href="/wiki/Rock_Your_Body" title="Rock Your Body">Rock Your Body</a>", soon switching over to "Can't Stop the Feeling!". He was joined by a group of backup singers/dancers and a horn section for the song's televised debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The performance wasn't aired in the US due to rights issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The day before the main show, Timberlake made his first appearance before an audience on night rehearsal to perform both songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chart_performance">Chart performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Chart performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Counting its first three days of airplay, "Can't Stop the Feeling!" debuted at No. 24 on the US <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a> and started at a personal-best No. 19 on <a href="/wiki/Adult_Top_40" title="Adult Top 40">Adult Top 40</a>, both for the charts dated May 21, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popdebut_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-popdebut-66">[66]</a></sup> "Can't Stop the Feeling!" became the first song in the history of <a href="/wiki/Mediabase" title="Mediabase">Mediabase</a> Top 40 to close the entire <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_hit_radio" title="Contemporary hit radio">Top 40</a> radio station panel in the first week, being the "most added" song in all 186 of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Can't Stop the Feeling!" became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">26th song to debut at No. 1</a> on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> on the chart issue dated May 28, 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hot100numberone_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-hot100numberone-3">[3]</a></sup> marking Justin Timberlake's fifth chart-topping single in the country. The song started at the Hot 100's summit powered most heavily by its No. 1 debut on the <a href="/wiki/Digital_Songs" title="Digital Songs">Digital Songs</a> sales chart (where it's Timberlake's sixth leader), having sold 379,000 downloads in its first week (ending May 12), according to Nielsen Music. Timberlake scored his highest weekly sales total for a song, besting the 315,000-unit start for "<a href="/wiki/Suit_%26_Tie" title="Suit &amp; Tie">Suit &amp; Tie</a>" in 2013. It entered <a href="/wiki/Streaming_Songs" title="Streaming Songs">Streaming Songs</a> at No. 6 with 15.6 million US streams in its first full week. On <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay_(Radio_Songs)" title="Hot 100 Airplay (Radio Songs)">Radio Songs</a>, it ascended 27-9 following its first full week of airplay (83 million in audience), becoming the first song to reach the Radio Songs top 10 in just two chart weeks since <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)" title="Hello (Adele song)">Hello</a>" (November 14, 2015). With "<a href="/wiki/Give_It_to_Me_(Timbaland_song)" title="Give It to Me (Timbaland song)">Give It to Me</a>" having last led the Hot 100 dated April 28, 2007, Timberlake returned to No. 1 after nine years and one month, the longest span between leaders since <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a> waited 10 years, two months and one week between "<a href="/wiki/Lady_Marmalade#Moulin_Rouge.21_version" title="Lady Marmalade">Lady Marmalade</a>" in 2001 and her featured turn on <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Moves_like_Jagger" title="Moves like Jagger">Moves like Jagger</a>" in 2011. Among males, it saw Timberlake end the longest break between Hot 100 No. 1s since <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> went 12 years, two months and three weeks between "<a href="/wiki/No_Diggity" title="No Diggity">No Diggity</a>" (by <a href="/wiki/Blackstreet" title="Blackstreet">Blackstreet</a> featuring Dr. Dre) and "<a href="/wiki/Crack_a_Bottle" title="Crack a Bottle">Crack a Bottle</a>", his collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> and <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hot100numberone_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-hot100numberone-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Can't Stop the Feeling!" reached No. 1 on <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay_(Radio_Songs)" title="Hot 100 Airplay (Radio Songs)">Radio Songs</a> in just its fifth week, marking the quickest sprint to the top since Adele's "Hello" needed just four weeks in November 2015. Among male artists, the single made the fastest rise to No. 1 on Radio Songs in nearly 25 years, since <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Black_or_White" title="Black or White">Black or White</a>" set the record with a three-week climb in 1991. <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_There_(The_Jackson_5_song)#Mariah_Carey_version" title="I'll Be There (The Jackson 5 song)">I'll Be There</a>" tied the mark in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The single also tied Adele's "Hello" for the fastest-ever rise to the top of the <a href="/wiki/Adult_Top_40" title="Adult Top 40">Adult Top 40</a>. Among males, "Feeling" bested <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a>' eight-week trip to the top with "<a href="/wiki/Happy_(Pharrell_Williams_song)" title="Happy (Pharrell Williams song)">Happy</a>", which reached No. 1 in April 2014, for the quickest climb to the top spot by a solo male artist. "Can't Stop the Feeling!" also reached the top of the <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a>, where Timberlake passed <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Mars" title="Bruno Mars">Bruno Mars</a> for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_artists_with_the_most_number_ones_on_the_Billboard_Mainstream_Top_40_chart" title="List of artists with the most number ones on the Billboard Mainstream Top 40 chart">most No. 1s</a> among males.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>With "Can't Stop the Feeling!" spending a sixth week atop <a href="/wiki/Digital_Songs" title="Digital Songs">Digital Songs</a>, it became Timberlake's longest lead atop the chart, passing "<a href="/wiki/SexyBack" title="SexyBack">SexyBack</a>". Additionally, it marked Timberlake's best weekly audience for a song with 163 million, passing the 159 million that "<a href="/wiki/Mirrors_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="Mirrors (Justin Timberlake song)">Mirrors</a>" drew at its peak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The following week, it became Timberlake's first solo No. 1 on <a href="/wiki/Adult_Contemporary_(chart)" title="Adult Contemporary (chart)">Adult Contemporary</a>. Reaching the AC summit in just its eighth week, "Feeling" completed the fastest run to No. 1 for a (non-holiday) song by a male artist in 17 years, since <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a>' "<a href="/wiki/You%27ll_Be_in_My_Heart" title="You'll Be in My Heart">You'll Be in My Heart</a>" needed only six frames in 1999. Among all songs, "Feeling" made the fastest trip to No. 1 on AC since Adele's "Hello": four weeks, in November 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Timberlake also earned his sixth number-one on <a href="/wiki/Dance_Club_Songs" title="Dance Club Songs">Dance Club Songs</a> with "Can't Stop the Feeling!". He reached the top of the chart without the aid of officially commissioned remixes. However, versions from Barry Harris, Fenix and Erick Decks, among others, have helped bring the song to club crowds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> "Can't Stop the Feeling!" became the eighth song to top Digital Songs for at least 10 weeks and the first since <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ronson" title="Mark Ronson">Mark Ronson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Uptown_Funk" title="Uptown Funk">Uptown Funk</a>" led for a record-tying 13 weeks in 2015; <a href="/wiki/Flo_Rida" title="Flo Rida">Flo Rida</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Low_(Flo_Rida_song)" title="Low (Flo Rida song)">Low</a>" first set the mark with 13 weeks at No. 1 on Digital Songs in 2007–08. "Feeling" is the second song to spend its first 10 weeks on Digital Songs at No. 1, joining <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">The Black Eyed Peas</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Boom_Boom_Pow" title="Boom Boom Pow">Boom Boom Pow</a>", which logged its first 10 weeks on the chart at the summit in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the US it was the best selling song of the summer, while being listed at 2 on the <i>Billboard</i> seasonal ranking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summer_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-summer-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a> named it the fifth most-streamed song of the summer globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> As of December 2016, it has sold 2.495 million downloads in the country, thus being the best selling song of the year according to Nielsen Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nielsen_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-nielsen-4">[4]</a></sup> It was also the No. 3 most-heard song on US radio in 2016, with 3.422 billion audience impressions for the year. It was the No. 2 most-played song in terms of total number of plays, with 587,000 detections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nielsen_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-nielsen-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>It reached the top position of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a> in its fifth week,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> after spending its first four weeks at number 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>By September 2016, it has been certified <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">quadruple platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-78">[78]</a></sup> and sextuple platinum by <a href="/wiki/Music_Canada" title="Music Canada">Music Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MC_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-MC-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe_and_Oceania">Europe and Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Europe and Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Can't Stop the Feeling!" reached the top spot in Belgium (Flanders and Wallonia), the Czech Republic, France, Germany, Israel, Scotland, Slovakia, Slovenia, Sweden, Switzerland, and the top 5 in Australia, Austria, Denmark, Greece, Hungary, Ireland, Latvia, Lebanon, the Netherlands, New Zealand, Norway, Poland, Portugal, Russia, Spain, and the United Kingdom. It spent four weeks atop the Euro Digital Songs chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The song debuted at number three on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>, and remained in the number 2 position for four weeks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> it later reached the top spot of the UK Singles Sales Chart and spent two weeks as well at the top position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Official_Charts_Company" title="Official Charts Company">Official Charts Company</a> from the UK named it Timberlake's biggest song in the country with over 1 million units sold, surpassing 2013's "<a href="/wiki/Mirrors_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="Mirrors (Justin Timberlake song)">Mirrors</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukhit_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-ukhit-6">[6]</a></sup> It was ranked 10 on UK year-end chart, while being the 3rd best selling song of the year in the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukyearend_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukyearend-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>By November 2016, it has been certified diamond by the <a href="/wiki/Syndicat_National_de_l%27%C3%89dition_Phonographique" title="Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique">Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snep_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-snep-84">[84]</a></sup> sextuple platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Swedish Recording Industry Association">Swedish Recording Industry Association</a> (GLF),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLF_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-GLF-85">[85]</a></sup> quintuple platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> (ARIA)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA-86">[86]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Federazione_Industria_Musicale_Italiana" title="Federazione Industria Musicale Italiana">Federazione Industria Musicale Italiana</a> (FIMI),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fimi_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-fimi-87">[87]</a></sup> double platinum by Denmark's <a href="/wiki/IFPI_Denmark" title="IFPI Denmark">IFPI</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ifpiden_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-ifpiden-88">[88]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Entertainment_Association" title="Belgian Entertainment Association">Belgian Entertainment Association</a> (BEA),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bea_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-bea-89">[89]</a></sup> and platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPI_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPI-90">[90]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recorded_Music_New_Zealand" title="Recorded Music New Zealand">Recorded Music New Zealand</a> (RMNZ),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RMNZ_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-RMNZ-91">[91]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Society_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="Polish Society of the Phonographic Industry">Polish Society of the Phonographic Industry</a> (ZVAP),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zvap_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-zvap-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_versions">Other versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lady_A_-_Charlotte_12-27-12-8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Lady_A_-_Charlotte_12-27-12-8.jpg/220px-Lady_A_-_Charlotte_12-27-12-8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Lady_A_-_Charlotte_12-27-12-8.jpg/330px-Lady_A_-_Charlotte_12-27-12-8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Lady_A_-_Charlotte_12-27-12-8.jpg/440px-Lady_A_-_Charlotte_12-27-12-8.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lady_A_-_Charlotte_12-27-12-8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lady_Antebellum" title="Lady Antebellum">Lady Antebellum</a> covered the song in a live performance.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The film version featured in the soundtrack album includes additional vocals from <a href="/wiki/Anna_Kendrick" title="Anna Kendrick">Anna Kendrick</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Corden" title="James Corden">James Corden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zooey_Deschanel" title="Zooey Deschanel">Zooey Deschanel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2016, American country music group <a href="/wiki/Lady_Antebellum" title="Lady Antebellum">Lady Antebellum</a> covered the song in a live performance in Columbus, Ohio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Jon Freeman of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> commented it "evoked the loose spirit of a jam band unwinding at a summer festival."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Charts">Charts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Can%27t_Stop_the_Feeling!&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Charts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
